office</th></tr><tr><th scope="row">Owner(s)</th><td>\nRangers Baseball Express, LLC (<a href="/wiki/Ray_Davis_(businessman)" title="Ray Davis (businessman)">Ray Davis</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bob_R._Simpson" title="Bob R. Simpson">Bob Simpson</a>, co-chairmen)<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup></td></tr><tr><th scope="row">Manager</th><td>\n<a href="/wiki/Vacant" class="mw-redirect" title="Vacant">Vacant</a></td></tr><tr><th scope="row">General Manager</th><td>\n<a href="/wiki/Jon_Daniels" title="Jon Daniels">Jon Daniels</a></td></tr><tr><th scope="row">President of Baseball Operations</th><td>\nJon Daniels</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>The <b>Texas Rangers</b> are an American <a href="/wiki/Professional_baseball" title="Professional baseball">professional baseball team</a> based in <a href="/wiki/Arlington,_Texas" title="Arlington, Texas">Arlington, Texas</a>, located in the <a href="/wiki/Dallas%E2%80%93Fort_Worth_metroplex" title="Dallas\xe2\x80\x93Fort Worth metroplex">Dallas&#8211;Fort Worth metroplex</a>. The Rangers franchise currently competes in <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball" title="Major League Baseball">Major League Baseball</a> (MLB) as a member of the <a href="/wiki/American_League" title="American League">American League</a> (AL) <a href="/wiki/American_League_West" title="American League West">West</a> division. Since <a href="/wiki/1994_Major_League_Baseball_season" title="1994 Major League Baseball season">1994</a>, the Rangers have played in <a href="/wiki/Globe_Life_Park_in_Arlington" title="Globe Life Park in Arlington">Globe Life Park in Arlington</a>. The team\'s name is borrowed from the famous <a href="/wiki/Texas_Ranger_Division" title="Texas Ranger Division">law enforcement agency</a> of the same name.\n</p><p>The franchise was established in 1961 as the <b>Washington Senators</b>, an <a href="/wiki/Expansion_team" title="Expansion team">expansion team</a> awarded to <a href="/wiki/Washington,_D.C." title="Washington, D.C.">Washington, D.C.</a>, after the city\'s first AL ballclub, the <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Washington_Senators_(1901%E2%80%9360)" title="History of the Washington Senators (1901\xe2\x80\x9360)">second Washington Senators</a>, moved to <a href="/wiki/Minnesota" title="Minnesota">Minnesota</a> and became the <a href="/wiki/Minnesota_Twins" title="Minnesota Twins">Twins</a> (the <a href="/wiki/Washington_Senators_(1891%E2%80%9399)" title="Washington Senators (1891\xe2\x80\x9399)">original Washington Senators</a> played primarily in the <a href="/wiki/National_League" title="National League">National League</a> during the 1890s). After the <a href="/wiki/1971_Major_League_Baseball_season" title="1971 Major League Baseball season">1971</a> season, the new Senators moved to Arlington, and debuted as the Rangers the following spring.\n</p><p>The Texas Rangers Baseball Club has made eight appearances in the MLB postseason, seven following division championships in 1996, 1998, 1999, 2010, 2011, 2015, and 2016 and as a <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball_wild_card" title="Major League Baseball wild card">wild card</a> team in 2012. In 2010, the Rangers advanced past the Division Series for the first time, defeating the <a href="/wiki/Tampa_Bay_Rays" title="Tampa Bay Rays">Tampa Bay Rays</a>. Texas then brought home their first <a href="/wiki/2010_American_League_Championship_Series" title="2010 American League Championship Series">American League pennant</a> after beating the <a href="/wiki/New_York_Yankees" title="New York Yankees">New York Yankees</a> in six games. In the <a href="/wiki/2010_World_Series" title="2010 World Series">2010 World Series</a>, the franchise\'s first, the Rangers fell to the <a href="/wiki/San_Francisco_Giants" title="San Francisco Giants">San Francisco Giants</a> in five games. They repeated as American League champions the following year, then lost the <a href="/wiki/2011_World_Series" title="2011 World Series">2011 World Series</a> to the <a href="/wiki/St._Louis_Cardinals" title="St. Louis Cardinals">St. Louis Cardinals</a> in seven games.\n</p>\n<div id="toc" class="toc"><input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" class="toctogglecheckbox" style="display:none" /><div class="toctitle" lang="en" dir="ltr"><h2>Contents</h2><span class="toctogglespan"><label class="toctogglelabel" for="toctogglecheckbox"></label></span></div>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-1"><a href="#History"><span class="tocnumber">1</span> <span class="toctext">History</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-17"><a href="#Roster"><span class="tocnumber">5</span> <span class="toctext">Roster</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-18"><a href="#Achievements"><span class="tocnumber">6</span> <span class="toctext">Achievements</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-19"><a href="#Baseball_Hall_of_Famers"><span class="tocnumber">6.1</span> <span class="toctext">Baseball Hall of Famers</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-20"><a href="#Ford_C._Frick_Award_recipients"><span class="tocnumber">6.2</span> <span class="toctext">Ford C. Frick Award recipients</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-21"><a href="#Texas_Sports_Hall_of_Fame"><span class="tocnumber">6.3</span> <span class="toctext">Texas Sports Hall of Fame</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-22"><a href="#Texas_Rangers_Hall_of_Fame"><span class="tocnumber">6.4</span> <span class="toctext">Texas Rangers Hall of Fame</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-23"><a href="#Retired_numbers"><span class="tocnumber">6.5</span> <span class="toctext">Retired numbers</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-24"><a href="#Team_captains"><span class="tocnumber">6.6</span> <span class="toctext">Team captains</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-25"><a href="#Team_records"><span class="tocnumber">7</span> <span class="toctext">Team records</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-26"><a href="#Texas_Rangers_Six_Shooters"><span class="tocnumber">8</span> <span class="toctext">Texas Rangers Six Shooters</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-27"><a href="#Minor_league_affiliations"><span class="tocnumber">9</span> <span class="toctext">Minor league affiliations</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-28"><a href="#See_also"><span class="tocnumber">10</span> <span class="toctext">See also</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-29"><a href="#References"><span class="tocnumber">11</span> <span class="toctext">References</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-30"><a href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">12</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Texas_Rangers_(baseball)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Texas_Rangers_(baseball)" title="History of the Texas Rangers (baseball)">History of the Texas Rangers (baseball)</a></div>\n<h3><span id="Washington_Senators_.281961.E2.80.931971.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Washington_Senators_(1961\xe2\x80\x931971)">Washington Senators (1961\xe2\x80\x931971)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Texas_Rangers_(baseball)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Washington Senators (1961\xe2\x80\x931971)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>When the second <a href="/wiki/Washington_Senators_(1901%E2%80%9360)" class="mw-redirect" title="Washington Senators (1901\xe2\x80\x9360)">Washington Senators</a> moved to <a href="/wiki/Minnesota" title="Minnesota">Minnesota</a> in 1960 to become the <a href="/wiki/Minnesota_Twins" title="Minnesota Twins">Twins</a>, Major League Baseball decided to expand a year earlier than planned to stave off the twin threats of competition from the proposed <a href="/wiki/Continental_League" title="Continental League">Continental League</a> and loss of its <a href="/wiki/Federal_Baseball_Club_v._National_League" title="Federal Baseball Club v. National League">exemption</a> from the <a href="/wiki/Sherman_Antitrust_Act" class="mw-redirect" title="Sherman Antitrust Act">Sherman Antitrust Act</a>. This new Senators team of the <a href="/wiki/American_League" title="American League">American League</a> adopted the old Senators name, but was (and still is) considered an expansion team since the Twins retained the old Senators\' records and history. The Senators and their expansion cousins, the <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_Angels" title="Los Angeles Angels">Los Angeles Angels</a> began to fill their rosters with American League players in an <a href="/wiki/1960_MLB_Expansion_Draft" class="mw-redirect" title="1960 MLB Expansion Draft">expansion draft</a>. The team played the <a href="/wiki/1961_Major_League_Baseball_season" title="1961 Major League Baseball season">1961</a> season at old <a href="/wiki/Griffith_Stadium" title="Griffith Stadium">Griffith Stadium</a> before moving to the new <a href="/wiki/District_of_Columbia_Stadium" class="mw-redirect" title="District of Columbia Stadium">District of Columbia Stadium</a> under a 10-year lease.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Richard_Nixon_throwing_out_opening_pitch_at_Senators_game,_1969.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/Richard_Nixon_throwing_out_opening_pitch_at_Senators_game%2C_1969.jpg/220px-Richard_Nixon_throwing_out_opening_pitch_at_Senators_game%2C_1969.jpg" width="220" height="269" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/Richard_Nixon_throwing_out_opening_pitch_at_Senators_game%2C_1969.jpg/330px-Richard_Nixon_throwing_out_opening_pitch_at_Senators_game%2C_1969.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/Richard_Nixon_throwing_out_opening_pitch_at_Senators_game%2C_1969.jpg/440px-Richard_Nixon_throwing_out_opening_pitch_at_Senators_game%2C_1969.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2515" data-file-height="3076" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Richard_Nixon_throwing_out_opening_pitch_at_Senators_game,_1969.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>U.S. President <a href="/wiki/Richard_Nixon" title="Richard Nixon">Richard Nixon</a> throwing <a href="/wiki/Opening_Day" title="Opening Day">Opening Day</a> <a href="/wiki/Ceremonial_first_pitch" title="Ceremonial first pitch">ceremonial first pitch</a> at <a href="/wiki/Robert_F._Kennedy_Memorial_Stadium" title="Robert F. Kennedy Memorial Stadium">RFK Stadium</a> on April 7, 1969, with <a href="/wiki/Ted_Williams" title="Ted Williams">Ted Williams</a> (left) and <a href="/wiki/Bob_Short" title="Bob Short">Bob Short</a> (right, partially obscured by <a href="/wiki/Ralph_Houk" title="Ralph Houk">Ralph Houk</a>)</div></div></div>\n<p>For most of their existence, the new Senators were the definition of futility, losing an average of 90 games a season. The team\'s struggles led to a twist on a joke about the old Senators: "Washington: <a href="/wiki/Henry_Lee_III#Political_career" title="Henry Lee III">first in war, first in peace</a> and <i>still</i> last in the American League." Their only winning season was in <a href="/wiki/1969_Major_League_Baseball_season" title="1969 Major League Baseball season">1969</a> when <a href="/wiki/Baseball_Hall_of_Fame" class="mw-redirect" title="Baseball Hall of Fame">Hall of Famer</a> <a href="/wiki/Ted_Williams" title="Ted Williams">Ted Williams</a> managed the club to an 86\xe2\x80\x9376 record, placing fourth in the AL East. <a href="/wiki/Frank_Howard_(baseball)" title="Frank Howard (baseball)">Frank Howard</a>, an <a href="/wiki/Outfielder" title="Outfielder">outfielder</a>/<a href="/wiki/First_baseman" title="First baseman">first baseman</a> from 1965 to 1972 known for his towering home runs, was the team\'s most accomplished player, winning two home run titles.\n</p><p>Ownership changed hands several times during the franchise\'s stay in Washington and was often plagued by poor decision-making and planning. Following their brief success in 1969, owner <a href="/wiki/Bob_Short" title="Bob Short">Bob Short</a>, was forced to make many questionable trades to lower the debt he had incurred to pay for the team. By the end of the <a href="/wiki/1970_Major_League_Baseball_season" title="1970 Major League Baseball season">1970</a> campaign, Short had issued an ultimatum: unless someone was willing to buy the Senators for $12 million (in comparison, the <a href="/wiki/New_York_Yankees" title="New York Yankees">New York Yankees</a> were sold in 1973 for $8.8 million), he would not proceed to renew the stadium lease and would move the team elsewhere.\n</p><p>Short was especially receptive to an offer brought up by <a href="/wiki/Arlington,_Texas" title="Arlington, Texas">Arlington, Texas</a>, mayor <a href="/wiki/Tom_Vandergriff" title="Tom Vandergriff">Tom Vandergriff</a>, who had been trying to obtain a major league sports team to play in the Metroplex for over a decade. Years earlier, <a href="/wiki/Charles_O._Finley" class="mw-redirect" title="Charles O. Finley">Charles O. Finley</a>, the owner of the <a href="/wiki/Kansas_City_Athletics" class="mw-redirect" title="Kansas City Athletics">Kansas City Athletics</a>, sought to relocate his baseball team to <a href="/wiki/Dallas,_Texas" class="mw-redirect" title="Dallas, Texas">Dallas, Texas</a>, but the idea was rebuffed and ultimately declined by the other AL team owners. Arlington\'s <a href="/wiki/Hole_card" class="mw-redirect" title="Hole card">hole card</a> was <a href="/wiki/Turnpike_Stadium" class="mw-redirect" title="Turnpike Stadium">Turnpike Stadium</a>, a 10,000-seat park which had been built in <a href="/wiki/1965_Major_League_Baseball_season" title="1965 Major League Baseball season">1965</a> to house the <a href="/wiki/Double-A_(baseball)" title="Double-A (baseball)">Double-A</a> <a href="/wiki/Dallas-Fort_Worth_Spurs" class="mw-redirect" title="Dallas-Fort Worth Spurs">Dallas-Fort Worth Spurs</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Texas_League" title="Texas League">Texas League</a>. Only minor excavations would be necessary to expand the park to accommodate major league crowds as it had been built to major league specifications. \n</p><p>Vandergriff\'s offer of a multimillion-dollar down payment prompted Short to make the move to Arlington. On September 21, 1971, by a vote of 10 to 2, American League owners granted approval to move the franchise to Arlington for the <a href="/wiki/1972_Major_League_Baseball_season" title="1972 Major League Baseball season">1972</a> season.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> Senators fans were livid. Enmity came to a head at the club\'s last game in Washington. Thousands of fans simply walked in without paying after the security guards left early, swelling the paid attendance of 14,460 to around 25,000, while fans unfurled a banner reading "SHORT STINKS". With the Senators leading 7\xe2\x80\x935 and two outs in the top of the ninth inning, several hundred youths stormed the field, raiding it for souvenirs. One man grabbed <a href="/wiki/First_base" class="mw-redirect" title="First base">first base</a> and ran off with it. With no security in sight and only three bases, <a href="/wiki/Umpire_(baseball)" title="Umpire (baseball)">umpire</a> crew chief <a href="/wiki/Jim_Honochick" title="Jim Honochick">Jim Honochick</a> forfeited the game to the New York Yankees.<sup id="cite_ref-sensforfeit_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sensforfeit-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> The nation\'s capital went with out Major League Baseball for 33&#160;years until the relocation of the <a href="/wiki/National_League" title="National League">National League</a>\'s <a href="/wiki/Montreal_Expos" title="Montreal Expos">Montreal Expos</a> who became the <a href="/wiki/Washington_Nationals" title="Washington Nationals">Washington Nationals</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span id="Texas_Rangers_.281972.E2.80.93present.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Texas_Rangers_(1972\xe2\x80\x93present)">Texas Rangers (1972\xe2\x80\x93present)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Texas_Rangers_(baseball)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Texas Rangers (1972\xe2\x80\x93present)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<h4><span id="First_years_in_Texas_.281972.E2.80.931984.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="First_years_in_Texas_(1972\xe2\x80\x931984)">First years in Texas (1972\xe2\x80\x931984)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Texas_Rangers_(baseball)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: First years in Texas (1972\xe2\x80\x931984)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:FrankLucchesiFlickr.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/FrankLucchesiFlickr.jpg/220px-FrankLucchesiFlickr.jpg" width="220" height="169" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/FrankLucchesiFlickr.jpg/330px-FrankLucchesiFlickr.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/FrankLucchesiFlickr.jpg/440px-FrankLucchesiFlickr.jpg 2x" data-file-width="767" data-file-height="589" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:FrankLucchesiFlickr.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Frank_Lucchesi" title="Frank Lucchesi">Frank Lucchesi</a>, Rangers manager from 1975 to 1977</div></div></div>\n<p>Prior to the <a href="/wiki/1972_Major_League_Baseball_season" title="1972 Major League Baseball season">1972 season</a>, improvements were made to Turnpike Stadium, which reopened as <a href="/wiki/Arlington_Stadium" title="Arlington Stadium">Arlington Stadium</a>, in preparation for the inaugural season of the Texas Rangers. The team played its first game on April 15, 1972, a 1\xe2\x80\x930 loss at the hands of the <a href="/wiki/California_Angels" class="mw-redirect" title="California Angels">California Angels</a>, their 1961 expansion cousins. The next day, the Rangers defeated the Angels, 5\xe2\x80\x931, for the club\'s first victory.\n</p><p>In 1974, the Rangers experienced their first winning season after finishing last in both 1972 and 1973. Under the ownership of <a href="/wiki/Brad_Corbett" title="Brad Corbett">Brad Corbett</a>, they finished second in the American League West with an 84\xe2\x80\x9376 record, behind the eventual <a href="/wiki/World_Series" title="World Series">World Series</a> champion <a href="/wiki/Oakland_Athletics" title="Oakland Athletics">Oakland Athletics</a>. The <a href="/wiki/1974_Texas_Rangers_season" title="1974 Texas Rangers season">1974 Rangers</a> are still the only MLB team to finish above .500 after two consecutive 100-loss seasons. <a href="/wiki/Mike_Hargrove" title="Mike Hargrove">Mike Hargrove</a> was awarded <a href="/wiki/American_League_Rookie_of_the_Year" class="mw-redirect" title="American League Rookie of the Year">American League Rookie of the Year</a>, <a href="/wiki/Billy_Martin" title="Billy Martin">Billy Martin</a> was named <a href="/wiki/AL_Manager_of_the_Year" class="mw-redirect" title="AL Manager of the Year">AL Manager of the Year</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jeff_Burroughs" title="Jeff Burroughs">Jeff Burroughs</a> won <a href="/wiki/AL_MVP" class="mw-redirect" title="AL MVP">AL MVP</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Ferguson_Jenkins" title="Ferguson Jenkins">Ferguson Jenkins</a> was named the <a href="/wiki/Sporting_News_Comeback_Player_of_the_Year_Award" title="Sporting News Comeback Player of the Year Award">Comeback Player of the Year</a> after winning 25 games, a club record to this day. The team posted winning records again from 1977 to 1979 but fell short of reaching the playoffs. The Rangers came very close to clinching a playoff spot in 1981, but wound up losing the first half of the AL West by one-and-a-half games to Oakland at the time of the <a href="/wiki/1981_Major_League_Baseball_strike" title="1981 Major League Baseball strike">players\' strike</a>. Texas went on to finish under .500 each season through 1985.\n</p><p>The Rangers faced an attendance problem for a few years in Texas, due in part to both the team\'s inconsistent performance and the oppressive heat and humidity that can encompass the area in the summer. Until the <a href="/wiki/Florida_Marlins" class="mw-redirect" title="Florida Marlins">Florida Marlins</a> arrived in 1993, Arlington Stadium was often the hottest stadium in the majors, with temperatures frequently topping 100&#160;&#176;F throughout the summer. So, the Rangers began playing most of their weekend games between May and September at night, a tradition that continues to this day.\n</p>\n<h4><span id="Valentine.2C_Ryan.2C_and_Bush_.281985.E2.80.931994.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Valentine,_Ryan,_and_Bush_(1985\xe2\x80\x931994)">Valentine, Ryan, and Bush (1985\xe2\x80\x931994)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Texas_Rangers_(baseball)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Valentine, Ryan, and Bush (1985\xe2\x80\x931994)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Nolan_Ryan_Tiger_Stadium_1990_CROP.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Nolan_Ryan_Tiger_Stadium_1990_CROP.jpg/220px-Nolan_Ryan_Tiger_Stadium_1990_CROP.jpg" width="220" height="254" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Nolan_Ryan_Tiger_Stadium_1990_CROP.jpg/330px-Nolan_Ryan_Tiger_Stadium_1990_CROP.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Nolan_Ryan_Tiger_Stadium_1990_CROP.jpg/440px-Nolan_Ryan_Tiger_Stadium_1990_CROP.jpg 2x" data-file-width="767" data-file-height="886" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Nolan_Ryan_Tiger_Stadium_1990_CROP.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Nolan_Ryan" title="Nolan Ryan">Nolan Ryan</a> pitched for the Rangers from 1989 to 1993.</div></div></div>\n<p>Manager <a href="/wiki/Bobby_Valentine" title="Bobby Valentine">Bobby Valentine</a> became steward over an influx of talent in the late 1980s and early 1990s. A winning season in 1986 was a shock to pundits and fans alike as the Rangers remained in the race for the American League pennant for the entire season. With a team consisting of stellar young rookies such as <a href="/wiki/Rub%C3%A9n_Sierra" title="Rub\xc3\xa9n Sierra">Rub\xc3\xa9n Sierra</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pete_Incaviglia" title="Pete Incaviglia">Pete Incaviglia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mitch_Williams_(baseball)" class="mw-redirect" title="Mitch Williams (baseball)">Mitch Williams</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bobby_Witt" title="Bobby Witt">Bobby Witt</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Edwin_Correa" class="mw-redirect" title="Edwin Correa">Edwin Correa</a>, the Rangers finished the season in second place with an 87\xe2\x80\x9375 record, just five games behind the division-champion Angels. The season marked a dramatic 25-win improvement over the 1985 season, which resulted in yet another last-place finish in the West. The signing of 41-year-old star pitcher <a href="/wiki/Nolan_Ryan" title="Nolan Ryan">Nolan Ryan</a> prior to the 1989 season allowed Ryan to reach his 5,000th <a href="/wiki/Strikeout" title="Strikeout">strikeout</a>, 300th <a href="/wiki/Win_(baseball)" class="mw-redirect" title="Win (baseball)">win</a>, and 6th and 7th <a href="/wiki/No-hitter" title="No-hitter">no-hitters</a> with the Rangers. Despite powerful lineups including the likes of <a href="/wiki/Juan_Gonz%C3%A1lez_(baseball)" title="Juan Gonz\xc3\xa1lez (baseball)">Juan Gonz\xc3\xa1lez</a>, Rub\xc3\xa9n Sierra, <a href="/wiki/Julio_Franco" title="Julio Franco">Julio Franco</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Rafael_Palmeiro" title="Rafael Palmeiro">Rafael Palmeiro</a> and a pitching staff that also included <a href="/wiki/Charlie_Hough" title="Charlie Hough">Charlie Hough</a>, Bobby Witt, <a href="/wiki/Kevin_Brown_(right-handed_pitcher)" title="Kevin Brown (right-handed pitcher)">Kevin Brown</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Kenny_Rogers_(baseball)" title="Kenny Rogers (baseball)">Kenny Rogers</a>, Valentine\'s Rangers never finished above second place and he was relieved of his duties during the 1992 season.\n</p><p>In April 1989, Rangers owner and oil tycoon <a href="/wiki/Eddie_Chiles" title="Eddie Chiles">Eddie Chiles</a>, sold the team to an investment group headed by <a href="/wiki/George_W._Bush" title="George W. Bush">George W. Bush</a> for $89 million.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> While his own equity in the team was a small one ($500,000), Bush was named Managing General Partner of the new ownership group. He increased his investment to $600,000 the following year.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> Bush left his position with the Rangers when he was elected <a href="/wiki/Governor_of_Texas" title="Governor of Texas">Governor of Texas</a> in 1994, and he sold his stake in the team in 1998.\n</p><p>During Bush\'s tenure, the Rangers and the City of Arlington decided to replace the aging Arlington Stadium with a new publicly funded stadium, at a cost of $193 million, financed by Arlington residents, through a sales tax increase. Ground was broken on October 30, 1991, on what would become The Ballpark in Arlington (now named <a href="/wiki/Globe_Life_Park_in_Arlington" title="Globe Life Park in Arlington">Globe Life Park in Arlington</a>).\n</p><p>In 1993, <a href="/wiki/Kevin_Kennedy_(baseball)" title="Kevin Kennedy (baseball)">Kevin Kennedy</a> took over managerial duties, presiding over the team for two seasons, keeping the 1993 Rangers in the hunt for a playoff berth into mid-September. Kennedy was let go in 1994, although the team led the AL West prior to the <a href="/wiki/1994%E2%80%9395_Major_League_Baseball_strike" title="1994\xe2\x80\x9395 Major League Baseball strike">players\' strike</a> which prompted commissioner <a href="/wiki/Bud_Selig" title="Bud Selig">Bud Selig</a> to cancel the remainder of the season and the playoffs. On July 28, Kenny Rogers pitched the 12th <a href="/wiki/Perfect_game" title="Perfect game">perfect game</a> in major league history in Arlington against the California Angels.\n</p>\n<h4><span id="First_division_titles_.281995.E2.80.932000.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="First_division_titles_(1995\xe2\x80\x932000)">First division titles (1995\xe2\x80\x932000)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Texas_Rangers_(baseball)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: First division titles (1995\xe2\x80\x932000)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Rangersballparkinarlington.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Rangersballparkinarlington.jpg/220px-Rangersballparkinarlington.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Rangersballparkinarlington.jpg/330px-Rangersballparkinarlington.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Rangersballparkinarlington.jpg/440px-Rangersballparkinarlington.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="768" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Rangersballparkinarlington.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Rangers Ballpark in Arlington opened in 1994.</div></div></div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Johnny_Oates" title="Johnny Oates">Johnny Oates</a> was hired as the Rangers\' manager in 1995. Oates and company helped to bring home the 1996 AL Western Division Championship, the first division championship in franchise history. The first playoff series, 24 years after the franchise came to Texas, saw the Rangers lose to the New York Yankees, 3 games to 1. Oates was named AL Manager of the Year and <a href="/wiki/Juan_Gonz%C3%A1lez_(baseball)" title="Juan Gonz\xc3\xa1lez (baseball)">Juan Gonz\xc3\xa1lez</a> was named AL MVP. The team featured a powerful lineup of hitters including Gonz\xc3\xa1lez, <a href="/wiki/Iv%C3%A1n_Rodr%C3%ADguez" title="Iv\xc3\xa1n Rodr\xc3\xadguez">Iv\xc3\xa1n Rodr\xc3\xadguez</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Rusty_Greer" title="Rusty Greer">Rusty Greer</a>, but continued to struggle with pitching despite having <a href="/wiki/Rick_Helling" title="Rick Helling">Rick Helling</a> and <a href="/wiki/Aaron_Sele" title="Aaron Sele">Aaron Sele</a> on their roster. Oates led the team to consecutive AL West championships in 1998 and 1999. Neither of Oates\' last two playoff teams could win a single game, losing all six in back-to-back sweeps at the hands of the Yankees, a team that won three World Series in the 1990s after defeating Rangers teams in the first round. The 1999 team was be the last playoff-bound team until 2010. En route to a second-straight last-place finish, Oates resigned his position 28&#160;games into the 2001 season.\n</p><p>In 1998, venture capital billionaire <a href="/wiki/Tom_Hicks" title="Tom Hicks">Tom Hicks</a> bought the team for $250 million.<sup id="cite_ref-test_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-test-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span id="The_lean_years_.282001.E2.80.932004.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="The_lean_years_(2001\xe2\x80\x932004)">The lean years (2001\xe2\x80\x932004)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Texas_Rangers_(baseball)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: The lean years (2001\xe2\x80\x932004)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Michael_Young_on_April_25,_2009.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Michael_Young_on_April_25%2C_2009.jpg/220px-Michael_Young_on_April_25%2C_2009.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Michael_Young_on_April_25%2C_2009.jpg/330px-Michael_Young_on_April_25%2C_2009.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Michael_Young_on_April_25%2C_2009.jpg/440px-Michael_Young_on_April_25%2C_2009.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3888" data-file-height="2592" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Michael_Young_on_April_25,_2009.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Michael_Young_(baseball)" title="Michael Young (baseball)">Michael Young</a> was selected for the <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball_All-Star_Game" title="Major League Baseball All-Star Game">MLB All-Star Game</a> seven times (2004\xe2\x80\x932009, 2011).</div></div></div>\n<p>Prior to the 2001 season, star free agent shortstop <a href="/wiki/Alex_Rodriguez" title="Alex Rodriguez">Alex Rodriguez</a> was signed by the Rangers in the most lucrative deal in baseball history: a 10-year, $252 million contract. The move was controversial and is frequently maligned by fans and writers who thought that owner Tom Hicks was placing too much emphasis on one player instead of utilizing team resources to acquire several players, especially for a team that lacked pitching talent. Club officials maintained that Rodriguez would be the cornerstone of future postseason success. Although Rodriguez\'s individual performance was outstanding, the Rangers continued to struggle, and manager <a href="/wiki/Jerry_Narron" title="Jerry Narron">Jerry Narron</a> was fired following the 2002 season and was replaced by seasoned manager <a href="/wiki/Buck_Showalter" title="Buck Showalter">Buck Showalter</a>. The 2003 season signified the Rangers\' fourth-straight last-place finish, and after a postseason fallout between Rodriguez and club management, the reigning AL MVP and newly appointed Rangers captain was traded to the New York Yankees for second baseman <a href="/wiki/Alfonso_Soriano" title="Alfonso Soriano">Alfonso Soriano</a> and infield prospect <a href="/wiki/Joaqu%C3%ADn_%C3%81rias_(baseball)" class="mw-redirect" title="Joaqu\xc3\xadn \xc3\x81rias (baseball)">Joaquin Arias</a>.\n</p><p>The Rangers battled with the <a href="/wiki/Anaheim_Angels" class="mw-redirect" title="Anaheim Angels">Anaheim Angels</a> and Oakland Athletics for first place in the AL West for much of the 2004 season. <a href="/wiki/Mark_Teixeira" title="Mark Teixeira">Mark Teixeira</a>, Alfonso Soriano, <a href="/wiki/Michael_Young_(baseball)" title="Michael Young (baseball)">Michael Young</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Hank_Blalock" title="Hank Blalock">Hank Blalock</a> became some of the best-hitting infielders in the league, with Young, Blalock, and Soriano being selected for the <a href="/wiki/2004_Major_League_Baseball_All-Star_Game" title="2004 Major League Baseball All-Star Game">2004 All-Star Game</a>. Soriano was named the All-Star MVP after going 2 for 3 with a three-run <a href="/wiki/Home_run" title="Home run">home run</a>. Despite a late-season push, the Rangers ended up losing six of their final ten games and finished in third place behind the Angels and A\'s, a mere three games out of first place.\n</p>\n<h4><span id="Making_changes_.282005.E2.80.932009.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Making_changes_(2005\xe2\x80\x932009)">Making changes (2005\xe2\x80\x932009)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Texas_Rangers_(baseball)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Making changes (2005\xe2\x80\x932009)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Nelson_Cruz.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/Nelson_Cruz.jpg/220px-Nelson_Cruz.jpg" width="220" height="278" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/Nelson_Cruz.jpg/330px-Nelson_Cruz.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/Nelson_Cruz.jpg/440px-Nelson_Cruz.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1888" data-file-height="2385" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Nelson_Cruz.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Nelson_Cruz" title="Nelson Cruz">Nelson Cruz</a>, Rangers outfielder from 2006 to 2013</div></div></div>\n<p>In 2005, the Rangers again struggled to find consistency amid controversy and injuries. <a href="/wiki/John_Hart_(baseball)" title="John Hart (baseball)">John Hart</a> stepped down as general manager following the 2005 season. <a href="/wiki/Jon_Daniels" title="Jon Daniels">Jon Daniels</a> was promoted from assistant general manager to replace him. Daniels, at 28 years and one month, became the youngest general manager in major league history.\n</p><p>Daniels and the Rangers front office were very active in acquiring new players before and during the 2006 season. New acquisitions included <a href="/wiki/Brad_Wilkerson" title="Brad Wilkerson">Brad Wilkerson</a>, <a href="/wiki/Adam_Eaton_(pitcher)" title="Adam Eaton (pitcher)">Adam Eaton</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kevin_Millwood" title="Kevin Millwood">Kevin Millwood</a>, <a href="/wiki/Carlos_Lee" title="Carlos Lee">Carlos Lee</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Nelson_Cruz" title="Nelson Cruz">Nelson Cruz</a>. Despite bolstering their roster, the Rangers\' 2006 season ended with a disappointing 80\xe2\x80\x9382 record and a third-place finish in the AL West. Buck Showalter was dismissed as manager after the season. The team hired Oakland third base coach <a href="/wiki/Ron_Washington" title="Ron Washington">Ron Washington</a> as their next mananger.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> A change at manager was the first of several moves to strengthen the team in yet another busy offseason. The team lost <a href="/wiki/Gary_Matthews,_Jr." class="mw-redirect" title="Gary Matthews, Jr.">Gary Matthews, Jr.</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mark_DeRosa" title="Mark DeRosa">Mark DeRosa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Carlos_Lee" title="Carlos Lee">Carlos Lee</a>, and Adam Eaton, but gained <a href="/wiki/Kenny_Lofton" title="Kenny Lofton">Kenny Lofton</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sammy_Sosa" title="Sammy Sosa">Sammy Sosa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Frank_Catalanotto" title="Frank Catalanotto">Frank Catalanotto</a>, and pitchers <a href="/wiki/%C3%89ric_Gagn%C3%A9" title="\xc3\x89ric Gagn\xc3\xa9">\xc3\x89ric Gagn\xc3\xa9</a> and <a href="/wiki/Brandon_McCarthy" title="Brandon McCarthy">Brandon McCarthy</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:D_Holland.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/D_Holland.jpg/220px-D_Holland.jpg" width="220" height="481" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/D_Holland.jpg/330px-D_Holland.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/f/f5/D_Holland.jpg 2x" data-file-width="422" data-file-height="922" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:D_Holland.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Derek_Holland" title="Derek Holland">Derek Holland</a>, one of the top pitching prospects to be drafted by Texas, pitched for the Rangers from 2009 to 2016.</div></div></div>\n<p>The Rangers struggled offensively early in the 2007 season, despite playing in a notoriously hitter-friendly park. A number of roster moves before the 2007 trade deadline were the beginnings of a rebuilding project headed by Jon Daniels with a focus on the acquisition and development of young players. In the coming years, more club resources would be dedicated to improving the quality of the farm system and scouting departments, most notably in Latin America and the Far East. Daniels\' objective was to field a legitimately competitive team by the 2010 season.\n</p><p>The Rangers began the 2008 season exceptionally well, headlined by newcomer <a href="/wiki/Josh_Hamilton" title="Josh Hamilton">Josh Hamilton</a> who looked to be a threat to win the <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball_Triple_Crown" class="mw-redirect" title="Major League Baseball Triple Crown">Triple Crown</a>, before fading off as the season wore on. During the All-Star festivities at <a href="/wiki/Yankee_Stadium_(1923)" title="Yankee Stadium (1923)">Yankee Stadium</a>, Hamilton crushed a first round home run record in the 2008 <a href="/wiki/Home_Run_Derby" title="Home Run Derby">Home Run Derby</a> with 28. Hamilton hit another four in the second round and three during the final round, for a total of 35 home runs, but lost to the Twins\' <a href="/wiki/Justin_Morneau" title="Justin Morneau">Justin Morneau</a>. Four Rangers played in the All Star Game: Hamilton, <a href="/wiki/Ian_Kinsler" title="Ian Kinsler">Ian Kinsler</a>, <a href="/wiki/Milton_Bradley_(baseball)" title="Milton Bradley (baseball)">Milton Bradley</a>, and Michael Young, who would repeat his 2006 All-Star Game feat by driving in the winning run via a sac fly.\n</p><p>The Rangers finished the season with yet another sub-.500 record (79\xe2\x80\x9383), yet ended the season second in the AL West, the club\'s best finish since 1999. The 2009 season saw the Rangers soar into playoff contention for the first time since 2004. Despite injuries to Josh Hamilton and <a href="/wiki/Ian_Kinsler" title="Ian Kinsler">Ian Kinsler</a>, the Rangers held first place in their division for long stretches of the summer before fading after September 1, losing the division to the Los Angeles Angels. The Rangers finished the season at 87\xe2\x80\x9375, their first winning season since 2004 and good enough for second place in the AL West. Michael Young responded to his move to third base by posting one of his best offensive seasons ever while committing just nine errors and earning a sixth-straight All-Star appearance.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> Josh Hamilton and <a href="/wiki/Nelson_Cruz" title="Nelson Cruz">Nelson Cruz</a> were also named 2009 AL All-Stars.\n</p>\n<h4><span id="Rangers_Baseball_Express.2C_LLC"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Rangers_Baseball_Express,_LLC">Rangers Baseball Express, LLC</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Texas_Rangers_(baseball)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Rangers Baseball Express, LLC">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>Following financial problems, including defaulting on a $525 million loan,<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Tom_Hicks" title="Tom Hicks">Tom Hicks</a> and Hicks Sports Group reached an agreement to sell the Texas Rangers to group headed by Pittsburgh sports lawyer <a href="/wiki/Chuck_Greenberg_(businessman)" title="Chuck Greenberg (businessman)">Chuck Greenberg</a> and Rangers team president Nolan Ryan for approximately $570 million on January 22, 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-mlb.mlb.com_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mlb.mlb.com-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> Hicks also sold much of the land surrounding Rangers Ballpark to Greenberg and Ryan\'s group in a separate deal.\n</p><p>However, one of HSG\'s principal lenders, <a href="/wiki/Monarch_Alternative_Capital" title="Monarch Alternative Capital">Monarch Alternative Capital</a>, opposed the sale on grounds that the proceeds would not fully repay the defaulted HSG notes.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> On April 21, Major League Baseball issued a statement declaring the Rangers\' sale to be under the control of the Commissioner to expedite the process.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> As the stalemate between HSG and its creditors continued, the Texas Rangers filed for <a href="/wiki/Chapter_11,_Title_11,_United_States_Code" title="Chapter 11, Title 11, United States Code">Chapter 11 bankruptcy</a> on May 24.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-blogs.wsj.com_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-blogs.wsj.com-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> As of that date, the Rangers and HSG had an estimated debt of $575 million.<sup id="cite_ref-blogs.wsj.com_21-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-blogs.wsj.com-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> Much of the unsecured debt was owed in back salary. Yankees third baseman Alex Rodriguez topped the list of unsecured creditors with an estimated $24.9 million owed by the Rangers.<sup id="cite_ref-blogs.wsj.com_21-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-blogs.wsj.com-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> The sale would repay all the team\'s creditors, including Rodriguez and other players owed back salary.<sup id="cite_ref-blogs.wsj.com_21-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-blogs.wsj.com-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> Following a court-ordered public auction to be held on August 4 with the winning bid submitted by Greenberg/Ryan, the bankruptcy court closed the case. The sale to Greenberg/Ryan was approved by all 30 MLB owners at the owners meeting in Minneapolis on August 12. The new ownership group was called Rangers Baseball Express, LLC and had Chuck Greenberg serving as managing general partner and Nolan Ryan as club president.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span id="Rise_to_contention_.282010.E2.80.932016.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Rise_to_contention_(2010\xe2\x80\x932016)">Rise to contention (2010\xe2\x80\x932016)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Texas_Rangers_(baseball)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Rise to contention (2010\xe2\x80\x932016)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>With the influx of talent and success in 2009, the Rangers entered the 2010 season expecting to compete for the division and achieve the front office\'s 2007 goals. During the off-season, Nolan Ryan spoke about the Rangers\' chances in the upcoming season saying, "My expectations today are that we\'re going to be extremely competitive and if we don\'t win our division, I\'ll be disappointed."<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Josh_Hamilton_2008_(1).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Josh_Hamilton_2008_%281%29.jpg/220px-Josh_Hamilton_2008_%281%29.jpg" width="220" height="330" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Josh_Hamilton_2008_%281%29.jpg/330px-Josh_Hamilton_2008_%281%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Josh_Hamilton_2008_%281%29.jpg/440px-Josh_Hamilton_2008_%281%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2592" data-file-height="3888" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Josh_Hamilton_2008_(1).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Josh_Hamilton" title="Josh Hamilton">Josh Hamilton</a> won the 2008 <a href="/wiki/League_Championship_Series_Most_Valuable_Player_Award" title="League Championship Series Most Valuable Player Award">ALCS MVP Award</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p>After stumbling out of the gates with a sub-.500 start in April 2010, the Rangers took the division lead with a franchise-best month of June, going 21\xe2\x80\x936. The Rangers never relinquished first place after an 11-game winning streak. The team made several mid-season moves to acquire players such as <a href="/wiki/Cliff_Lee" title="Cliff Lee">Cliff Lee</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bengie_Molina" title="Bengie Molina">Bengie Molina</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jorge_Cant%C3%BA" title="Jorge Cant\xc3\xba">Jorge Cant\xc3\xba</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Jeff_Francoeur" title="Jeff Francoeur">Jeff Francoeur</a>. After the All-Star Game, in which six Rangers were present, came the debut of the claw and antler hand gestures, which gained much popularity, especially after the release of various apparel and souvenir options. Foam claws and helmets with deer antlers became quite commonplace in the ballpark as the Rangers played further into the fall. The Rangers won the AL West on September 25, advancing to the postseason for the first time since 1999 with a 90\xe2\x80\x9372 record.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> The Rangers entered the playoffs against the <a href="/wiki/Tampa_Bay_Rays" title="Tampa Bay Rays">Tampa Bay Rays</a> in the first round, which ultimately resulted in a 3\xe2\x80\x932 series victory and marked the first postseason series victory in the 50-year history of the Rangers/Washington Senators franchise. Facing the Rangers in the American League Championship Series were the defending World Champion New York Yankees, the team the Rangers failed against three separate times in the 1990s. In a six-game ALCS, Texas came out victorious, winning the first pennant in franchise history in front of an ecstatic home crowd.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> Josh Hamilton was awarded <a href="/wiki/League_Championship_Series_Most_Valuable_Player_Award" title="League Championship Series Most Valuable Player Award">ALCS MVP</a>. The Texas Rangers faced the <a href="/wiki/San_Francisco_Giants" title="San Francisco Giants">San Francisco Giants</a> in the <a href="/wiki/2010_World_Series" title="2010 World Series">2010 World Series</a>, but their offense struggled against the Giants\' young pitching and eventually lost the Series, 4\xe2\x80\x931.\n</p><p>In March 2011, Chick Greenberg resigned as Chief Executive and Managing General Partner and sold his interest in the Club after a falling out with his partners.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated3_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated3-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> Following his resignation, Nolan Ryan was named Chief Executive Officer in addition to his continuing role as Team President.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> Ryan was subsequently designated the Controlling Owner of the Club by a unanimous vote of the 30 owners of Major League Baseball on May 12.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated3_26-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated3-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Rangers successfully defended their AL West Division title in 2011, making the club\'s second-straight division title and postseason appearance. The Rangers set records for best win\xe2\x80\x93loss record (96\xe2\x80\x9366, .592) and home attendance (2,946,949). On October 15, they went back to the <a href="/wiki/2011_World_Series" title="2011 World Series">2011 World Series</a> after beating the Detroit Tigers 15\xe2\x80\x935 in game six of the ALCS.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> The series featured Nelson Cruz hitting six home runs, the most home runs by one player in a playoff series in MLB history. In game two, Cruz also became the first player in postseason history to win a game with a walk-off grand slam as the Rangers defeated the Tigers 7\xe2\x80\x933 in 11 innings. However, they proceeded to lose to the <a href="/wiki/St._Louis_Cardinals" title="St. Louis Cardinals">St. Louis Cardinals</a> in seven games, after twice being one strike away from the championship in game six.\n</p><p>The Rangers dominated the American League standings for much of the 2012 season, but floundered in September, culminating in a sweep by the Oakland Athletics in the final series. They did, however, qualify for the first American League <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball_wild-card_game" class="mw-redirect" title="Major League Baseball wild-card game">wild-card playoff game</a>. In the new <a href="/wiki/2012_American_League_Wild_Card_Game" title="2012 American League Wild Card Game">Wild Card Game</a>, the Rangers\' woes continued, as they lost 5\xe2\x80\x931 to the Orioles. The Rangers figured in the 2013 wild card as well. They finished the season in second place in the American League West with a 91\xe2\x80\x9372 record, tied with the <a href="/wiki/Tampa_Bay_Rays" title="Tampa Bay Rays">Tampa Bay Rays</a> for a wild card spot. A 163rd play-in <a href="/wiki/2013_American_League_Wild_Card_tie-breaker_game" title="2013 American League Wild Card tie-breaker game">tie-breaker game</a> was held to determine the second participant in the <a href="/wiki/2013_American_League_Wild_Card_Game" title="2013 American League Wild Card Game">2013 American League Wild Card Game</a> against the <a href="/wiki/Cleveland_Indians" title="Cleveland Indians">Cleveland Indians</a>. The Rangers lost to the Rays, 5\xe2\x80\x932, in the tie-breaker and were eliminated from playoff contention after reaching the postseason in three consecutive seasons. Nolan Ryan stepped down as Rangers CEO effective October 31, 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Cole_Hamels_2018.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Cole_Hamels_2018.jpg/220px-Cole_Hamels_2018.jpg" width="220" height="311" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Cole_Hamels_2018.jpg/330px-Cole_Hamels_2018.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Cole_Hamels_2018.jpg/440px-Cole_Hamels_2018.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1669" data-file-height="2361" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Cole_Hamels_2018.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Cole_Hamels" title="Cole Hamels">Cole Hamels</a> was named the <a href="/wiki/Opening_Day" title="Opening Day">Opening Day</a> starter for the 2016 season.</div></div></div>\n<p>Injuries took a major toll on the Rangers in 2014 and 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> The lone bright spot was <a href="/wiki/Adri%C3%A1n_Beltr%C3%A9" title="Adri\xc3\xa1n Beltr\xc3\xa9">Adri\xc3\xa1n Beltr\xc3\xa9</a>, who despite spending some time injured, was the most consistent offensive player on the team.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> With the acquisition of <a href="/wiki/Cole_Hamels" title="Cole Hamels">Cole Hamels</a> in 2015, the Rangers overtook the <a href="/wiki/Houston_Astros" title="Houston Astros">Houston Astros</a> to clinch the American League West title on the final day of the season with a record of 88\xe2\x80\x9374. The Rangers went on to lose to the <a href="/wiki/Toronto_Blue_Jays" title="Toronto Blue Jays">Toronto Blue Jays</a> in five games in the <a href="/wiki/2015_American_League_Division_Series" title="2015 American League Division Series">Division Series</a> after squandering a 2\xe2\x80\x930 series lead. Texas again clinched the AL West in 2016, but lost to Toronto, 3\xe2\x80\x930, in the ALDS.\n</p>\n<h4><span id="2017.E2.80.93present"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2017\xe2\x80\x93present">2017\xe2\x80\x93present</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Texas_Rangers_(baseball)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: 2017\xe2\x80\x93present">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>The Rangers finished the 2017 campaign 23&#160;games out of first place with a 78\xe2\x80\x9384 record. On September 21, 2018, holding on to a 64\xe2\x80\x9388 record, the Rangers fired <a href="/wiki/Jeff_Banister" title="Jeff Banister">Jeff Banister</a> who had led the team since 2015. He was replaced by bench coach <a href="/wiki/Don_Wakamatsu" title="Don Wakamatsu">Don Wakamatsu</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Season-by-season_records">Season-by-season records</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span style="background-color:#C02126;color:#FFFFFF;">\xe2\x80\x94\n</th></tr></tbody></table>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Radio_and_television">Radio and television</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Texas_Rangers_(baseball)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Radio and television">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Texas_Rangers_broadcasters" title="List of Texas Rangers broadcasters">List of Texas Rangers broadcasters</a></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Radio">Radio</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Texas_Rangers_(baseball)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Radio">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/KRLD-FM" title="KRLD-FM">KRLD-FM</a> 105.3 FM</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/KRLD_(AM)" title="KRLD (AM)">KRLD (AM)</a> NewsRadio 1080 will carry any games that conflict with previously scheduled programming on 105.3 The FAN.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/KFLC" title="KFLC">KFLC</a> 1270 AM (<i>Spanish</i>)</li></ul>\n<p>In addition to the flagship stations listed above, Rangers games can be heard on affiliates throughout much of Texas, and also in parts of Oklahoma, Arkansas, Louisiana, and New Mexico.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Eric_Nadel" title="Eric Nadel">Eric Nadel</a> is the primary play-by-play announcer. He has called games for the club since 1979 beginning on television broadcasts, then moving exclusively to radio beginning in 1985. He became the primary announcer after the late <a href="/wiki/Mark_Holtz" title="Mark Holtz">Mark Holtz</a> moved to television. Currently, Nadel provides play-by-play in the 1st, 2nd, 5th, 6th, 8th, and 9th innings, and color commentary for the other innings. On December 11, 2013, he was awarded the 2014 <a href="/wiki/Ford_C._Frick_Award" title="Ford C. Frick Award">Ford C. Frick Award</a> by the <a href="/wiki/National_Baseball_Hall_of_Fame_and_Museum" title="National Baseball Hall of Fame and Museum">National Baseball Hall of Fame and Museum</a> for excellence in broadcasting.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Matt_Hicks" title="Matt Hicks">Matt Hicks</a> now shares the broadcast booth with Nadel. He joined the broadcast in 2012 after <a href="/wiki/Steve_Busby" title="Steve Busby">Steve Busby</a> moved from radio to television to replace <a href="/wiki/Dave_Barnett" title="Dave Barnett">Dave Barnett</a>. Hicks provides play-by-play in the 3rd, 4th, and 7th innings, and color commentary for the other innings. Jared Sandler hosts the pre-game and post-game shows, and also fills in whenever Nadel or Hicks have a day off. For the Spanish radio affiliates, Eleno Ornelas is the play-by-play announcer, and former Rangers pitcher <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Guzm%C3%A1n" title="Jos\xc3\xa9 Guzm\xc3\xa1n">Jos\xc3\xa9 Guzm\xc3\xa1n</a> is the color analyst.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Television">Television</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Texas_Rangers_(baseball)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Television">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Texas Rangers games currently air on regional television network <a href="/wiki/Fox_Sports_Southwest" title="Fox Sports Southwest">Fox Sports Southwest</a>. During the 2016 season, they had an average 3.96 rating and 105,000 viewers on primetime broadcasts.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> Due to the Rangers having to play many of their Sunday home games at night, the team has been featured frequently on <a href="/wiki/ESPN" title="ESPN">ESPN</a>\'s <i><a href="/wiki/Sunday_Night_Baseball" title="Sunday Night Baseball">Sunday Night Baseball</a></i> during the summer months. Rangers games can also be seen on <a href="/wiki/MLB_on_Fox" class="mw-redirect" title="MLB on Fox">MLB on Fox</a> and <a href="/wiki/TBS_(U.S._TV_channel)" title="TBS (U.S. TV channel)">TBS</a>. \n</p><p>Since 2017, <a href="/wiki/Dave_Raymond" title="Dave Raymond">Dave Raymond</a> is the primary television play-by-play announcer and former MLB pitcher <a href="/wiki/C._J._Nitkowski" title="C. J. Nitkowski">C. J. Nitkowski</a> is the primary color commentator.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> Nitkowski also fills in for Raymond on play-by-play for select games. Raymond replaced Steve Busby, who since 1982 on both TV and radio has had various stints in various positions on Rangers broadcasts from play-by-play to color commentary to pre-game and post-game analysis. In June 2012, Busby moved back to television play-by-play after <a href="/wiki/Dave_Barnett" title="Dave Barnett">Dave Barnett</a> left his position as game announcer following an episode in which he experienced speech difficulties.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> Beginning in 2016, Raymond substituted for Busby on select games. Previously the primary color commentator, <a href="/wiki/Tom_Grieve" title="Tom Grieve">Tom Grieve</a> still broadcasts many games. A former Rangers player and general manager, Grieve has been in the TV booth since 1995, following the end of his tenure as GM. Another former Ranger, <a href="/wiki/Mark_McLemore" title="Mark McLemore">Mark McLemore</a>, has substituted for Grieve in the past<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> and often joins the booth for an inning during home games. He and former Ranger <a href="/wiki/Iv%C3%A1n_Rodr%C3%ADguez" title="Iv\xc3\xa1n Rodr\xc3\xadguez">Iv\xc3\xa1n Rodr\xc3\xadguez</a> are among the pre-game and post-game analysts used on Fox Sports Southwest. FSSW pre-game and post-game shows are hosted by a rotation among Dana Larson, John Rhadigan, Ric Renner, and Erin Hartigan. In-game reporters include Rhadigan, Hartigan, Lesley McCaslin, and Rangers employee Emily Jones (formerly of FSSW).\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Mascot">Mascot</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Texas_Rangers_(baseball)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Mascot">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Rangers_Captain_team_mascot_May_23_2016.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Rangers_Captain_team_mascot_May_23_2016.jpg/220px-Rangers_Captain_team_mascot_May_23_2016.jpg" width="220" height="223" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Rangers_Captain_team_mascot_May_23_2016.jpg/330px-Rangers_Captain_team_mascot_May_23_2016.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Rangers_Captain_team_mascot_May_23_2016.jpg/440px-Rangers_Captain_team_mascot_May_23_2016.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2629" data-file-height="2665" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Rangers_Captain_team_mascot_May_23_2016.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Rangers Captain (May 2016)</div></div></div>\n<p>Rangers Captain is the mascot for the Texas Rangers. Introduced in 2002, he is a <a href="/wiki/Palomino" title="Palomino">palomino</a>-style horse, dressed in the team\'s uniform. He wears the uniform number 72 in honor of 1972, the year the Rangers relocated to Arlington. He has multiple uniforms to match each of the variants the team wears. Captain\'s outfits sometimes match a theme the team is promoting; on April 24, 2010, he was dressed up like <a href="/wiki/Elvis_Presley" title="Elvis Presley">Elvis Presley</a> as part of an Elvis themed night.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Roster">Roster</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Texas_Rangers_(baseball)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Roster">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" Greenville, attended University of Texas-Austin\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Texas_Rangers_Hall_of_Fame">Texas Rangers Hall of Fame</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Texas_Rangers_(baseball)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Texas Rangers Hall of Fame">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">"Texas Rangers Hall of Fame" redirects here. For the law enforcement agency, see <a href="/wiki/Texas_Ranger_Hall_of_Fame_and_Museum" title="Texas Ranger Hall of Fame and Museum">Texas Ranger Hall of Fame and Museum</a>.</div>\n<p>The <b>Texas Rangers <a href="/wiki/Hall_of_Fame" class="mw-redirect" title="Hall of Fame">Hall of Fame</a></b> was created in 2003 to honor the careers of former Texas Rangers players, managers, executives, and broadcasters. There are currently 20 members. The Hall is located in <a href="/wiki/Globe_Life_Park_in_Arlington" title="Globe Life Park in Arlington">Globe Life Park in Arlington</a>, behind right field. The Hall\'s two levels cover 13,000 square feet and included a 235-seat theater and various plaques, photos, and memorabilia. It can accommodate up to 600 people.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable">\n<caption>Key\n</caption>\n<tbody><tr>\n<th scope="row">Year\n</th>\n<td>Year inducted\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row" style="background:#ffb;"><b>Bold</b>\n</th>\n<td>Member of the <a href="/wiki/National_Baseball_Hall_of_Fame_and_Museum" title="National Baseball Hall of Fame and Museum">Baseball Hall of Fame</a>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row" style="background:#ffb;"><div class="center" style="width:auto; margin-left:auto; margin-right:auto;"><img alt="dagger" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/3/37/Dagger-14-plain.png" width="9" height="14" data-file-width="9" data-file-height="14" /></div>\n</th>\n<td>Member of the Baseball Hall of Fame as a Ranger\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row" style="background:#cfc;"><b>Bold</b>\n</th>\n<td>Recipient of the Hall of Fame\'s <a href="/wiki/Ford_C._Frick_Award" title="Ford C. Frick Award">Ford C. Frick Award</a>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<table class="wikitable" style="text-align:center">\n\n<tbody><tr>\n<td colspan="5" style="background-color:#233974;color:#FFFFFF;;"><b>Texas Rangers Hall class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Texas_Rangers_(baseball)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Texas Rangers Six Shooters">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>The Texas Rangers Six Shooters is an interactive dance squad for the Texas Rangers that perform various duties at Rangers home games. The women dance, tumble, and interact with fans.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> \n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline"
